| Goal | Tool |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Firefox DOM Event Dispatch Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a DOM event (e.g., click) is dispatched through the Firefox event system in mozilla/gecko-dev. Find C++ source files implementing: the event creation, the event target identification, the capture/bubble phase traversal, the event listener invocation, and the default action execution.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

I am thinking...: Now I have a comprehensive understanding of the Firefox DOM event dispatch chain. Let me summarize the key files and functions:

1. **Event Creation**: 
   - `dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp` - `EventDispatcher::CreateEvent()` creates DOM events from WidgetEvents
   - `dom/events/MouseEvent.cpp` / `dom/events/MouseEvent.h` - MouseEvent class
   - `widget/MouseEvents.h` - WidgetMouseEvent (the native event)

2. **Event Target Identification**:
   - `layout/base/PresShell.cpp` - `PresShell::HandleEvent()` receives the raw event and identifies the target frame
   - `layout/base/PresShell.cpp` - `PresShell::GetEventTargetContent()` gets the content node for the event
   - `layout/base/PresShell.cpp` - `PresShell::EventHandler::DispatchEventToDOM()` identifies the DOM event target
   - `dom/base/FragmentOrElement.cpp` - `nsIContent::GetEventTargetParent()` builds the event target chain

3. **Capture/Bubble Phase Traversal**:
   - `dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp` - `EventDispatcher::Dispatch()` - main dispatch function
   - `dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp` - `EventTargetChainItem::HandleEventTargetChain()` - handles capture, target, and bubble phases
   - `dom/events/EventDispatcher.h` - `EventChainPreVisitor`, `EventChainPostVisitor` - visitor classes

4. **Event Listener Invocation**:
   - `dom/events/EventListenerManager.cpp` - `EventListenerManager::HandleEventInternal()` - finds and calls listeners
   - `dom/events/EventListenerManager.cpp` - `EventListenerManager::HandleEventWithListenerArray()` - iterates through listeners
   - `dom/events/EventListenerManager.cpp` - `EventListenerManager::HandleEventSingleListener()` - invokes a single listener

5. **Default Action Execution**:
   - `layout/base/PresShell.cpp` - `PresShell::EventHandler::DispatchEvent
... (truncated)

Here is the complete trace of the Firefox DOM event dispatch chain for a click event through the C++ source:

---

## Firefox DOM Event Dispatch Chain

### Phase 1 — Event Creation

| File | Key Symbol |
|------|-----------|
| `widget/MouseEvents.h` | `WidgetMouseEvent` — the native event struct created by the widget layer |
| `dom/events/MouseEvent.h/.cpp` | `MouseEvent` — the DOM-level wrapper |
| `dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp` | `EventDispatcher::CreateEvent()` — lazily wraps a `WidgetEvent` into a DOM `Event` object during dispatch, switching on `mClass` (e.g., `eMouseEventClass` → `NS_NewDOMMouseEvent`) |

---

### Phase 2 — Event Target Identification

**File: `layout/base/PresShell.cpp`**

The raw `WidgetGUIEvent` arrives from the widget layer at:
```
PresShell::HandleEvent()
  → PresShell::EventHandler::HandleEvent()
    → PresShell::EventHandler::HandleEventWithTarget()
      → PresShell::GetEventTargetContent()   // resolves the nsIContent* under the cursor
      → PresShell::EventHandler::DispatchEvent()
```

`DispatchEvent()` is the orchestrator: it calls `EventStateManager::PreHandleEvent()`, then `DispatchEventToDOM()`, then `EventStateManager::PostHandleEvent()`.

---

### Phase 3 — Event Target Chain Construction (the capture/bubble path)

**File: `dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp`** — `EventDispatcher::Dispatch()`

After receiving the target node, `Dispatch()` builds a `nsTArray<EventTargetChainItem>` by repeatedly calling `GetEventTargetParent()` on each node walking up the tree:

| File | `GetEventTargetParent()` override | Role |
|------|----------------------------------|------|
| `dom/base/FragmentOrElement.cpp` | `nsIContent::GetEventTargetParent()` | Sets `mParentTarget` to the DOM parent node; handles shadow-tree retargeting and chrome-only subt

## What Was Traced

The complete Firefox DOM event dispatch chain for a click event, covering all 5 requested phases:

### 1. Event Creation
- **`widget/MouseEvents.h`** — `WidgetMouseEvent`: the native event struct created by the widget layer with message `ePointerClick`/`eMouseUp`

- **`dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp`** — `EventDispatcher::CreateEvent()`: lazily wraps a `WidgetEvent` into a DOM `Event` by switching on `mClass` (e.g., `eMouseEventClass` → `NS_NewDOMMouseEvent`)

### 2. Event Target Identification
- **`layout/base/PresShell.cpp`** — `PresShell::HandleEvent()` → `EventHandler::HandleEvent()` → `HandleEventWithTarget()` → `GetEventTargetContent()`: resolves the `nsIContent*` node under the cursor from the hit-tested layout frame, then `EventHandler::DispatchEvent()` orchestrates the full pre/dispatch/post sequence

### 3. Capture/Bubble Phase Traversal
- **`dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp`** — `EventDispatcher::Dispatch()` builds a `nsTArray<EventTargetChainItem>` by calling `GetEventTargetParent()` up the tree:
  - `nsIContent::GetEventTargetParent()` (**`dom/base/FragmentOrElement.cpp`**) — walks DOM parent nodes, handles shadow-tree retargeting
  - `Document::GetEventTargetParent()` (**`dom/base/Document.cpp`**) — sets parent to `nsGlobalWindowInner`
  - `nsGlobalWindowInner::GetEventTargetParent()` (**`dom/base/nsGlobalWindowInner.cpp`**) — sets parent to `nsWindowRoot`
  - `nsWindowRoot::GetEventTargetParent()` (**`dom/base/nsWindowRoot.cpp`**) — terminates the chain
  - `ShadowRoot::GetEventTargetParent()` (**`dom/base/

several C++ source files across `dom/events/`, `layout/base/`, and `dom/base/`. Here is the complete flow:\\n\\n### 1. Event Creation\\n\\nA click event originates as a `WidgetMouseEvent` (defined in `widget/MouseEvents.h`). When the widget layer receives a native mouse click, it creates a `WidgetMouseEvent` with message `ePointerClick` (or `eMouseUp` leading to a click). The corresponding DOM-level `MouseEvent` object (in `dom/events/MouseEvent.cpp` / `dom/events/MouseEvent.h`) is created lazily during dispatch via `EventDispatcher::CreateEvent()` in `dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp`.\\n\\n### 2. Event Target Identification\\n\\nThe raw event enters the Gecko event system through `PresShell::HandleEvent()` in `layout/base/PresShell.cpp`. This function:\\n- Receives the `WidgetGUIEvent` from the widget layer\\n- Delegates to `PresShell::EventHandler::HandleEvent()` and then `PresShell::EventHandler::HandleEventWithTarget()`\\n- Calls `PresShell::GetEventTargetContent()` to identify the DOM content node (element) under the cursor\\n- Stores the target frame and content in `mCurrentEventTarget`\\n\\nThen `PresShell::EventHandler::DispatchEvent()` is called, which:\\n1. Calls `EventStateManager::PreHandleEvent()` for pre-dispatch processing\\n2. Calls `PresShell::EventHandler::DispatchEventToDOM()` to identify the final DOM target node and call `EventDispatcher::Dispatch()`\\n\\n### 3. Event Target Chain Construction (Capture/Bubble Path)\\n\\nInside `EventDispatcher::Dispatch()` (`dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp`), the event target chain is built:\\n- An `EventTargetChainItem` is created for the initial target\\n- `EventTargetChainItem::GetEventTargetParent()` is called on each target, which calls `EventTarget::GetEventTargetParent()` on the DOM node\\n- For content nodes, `nsIContent::GetEventTargetParent()` (in `dom/base/FragmentOrElement.cpp`) sets `mParentTarget` to the parent node, building the chain upward through the DOM tree\\n- For `Document`, `Document::GetEventTargetParent()` (`dom/base/Document.cpp`) sets the parent to the inner window\\n- For `nsGlobalWindowInner`, `nsGlobalWindowInner::GetEventTargetParent()` (`dom/base/nsGlobalWindowInner.cpp`) sets the parent to the window root\\n- For `nsWindowRoot`, `nsWindowRoot::GetEventTargetParent()` (`dom/base/nsWindowRoot.cpp`) terminates the chain\\n- Shadow DOM boundaries are handled by `ShadowRoot::GetEventTargetParent()` (`dom/base/ShadowRoot.cpp`)\\n\\nThe chain is stored as a `nsTArray<EventTargetChainItem>` where index 0 is the innermost target and the last element is the outermost (window root).\\n\\n### 4. Capture, Target, and Bubble Phase Traversal\\n\\n`EventTargetChainItem::HandleEventTargetChain()` (`dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp`) implements the three-phase traversal:\\n\\n**Capture phase**: Iterates from the end of the chain (outermost) down to just above the target (`firstCanHandleEventTargetIdx`), calling `item.HandleEvent()` with `mInCapturePhase=true`.\\n\\n**Target phase**: Calls `targetItem.HandleEvent()` twice \u2014 once for capture listeners and once for bubble listeners at the target node itself.\\n\\n**Bubble phase**: Iterates from the target upward to the outermost node, calling `item.HandleEvent()` with `mInBubblingPhase=true` (only if the event bubbles).\\n\\nAfter the default event group, the chain is traversed again for the **system event group** (chrome/privileged listeners), with `mInSystemGroup=true`. During the system group pass, `PostHandleEvent()` is called on each item.\\n\\n### 5. Event Listener Invocation\\n\\nAt each node in the chain, `EventTargetChainItem::HandleEvent()` calls `EventListenerManager::HandleEvent()` (via `mManager->HandleEvent()`). This leads to:\\n\\n- `EventListenerManager::HandleEventInternal()` (`dom/events/EventListenerManager.cpp`): Looks up listeners by event type atom, calls `HandleEventWithListenerArray()` for matching listeners\\n- `EventListenerManager::HandleEventWithListenerArray()`: Iterates through the `ListenerArray`, checking phase (capture vs. bubble), trust level, and `once` flags\\n- `EventListenerManager::HandleEventSingleListener()`: Invokes the actual listener \u2014 either a WebIDL callback (`listenerHolder.GetWebIDLCallback()->HandleEvent()`) or an XPCOM callback (`listenerHolder.GetXPCOMCallback()->HandleEvent()`). This is where JavaScript event handlers are called.\\n\\nPropagation can be stopped at any point via `event.stopPropagation()` (sets `mPropagationStopped`) or `event.stopImmediatePropagation()` (sets `mImmediatePropagationStopped`).\\n\\n### 6. Default Action Execution\\n\\nDefault actions are handled in two ways:\\n\\n**Via `EventStateManager::PostHandleEvent()`** (`dom/events/EventStateManager.cpp`): Called by `PresShell::EventHandler::DispatchEvent()` after DOM dispatch. Handles default behaviors like focus changes on `eMouseDown`, link navigation, form submission triggers, etc.\\n\\n**Via `ActivationBehavior()`**: For elements that implement the HTML activation behavior (buttons, inputs, links), `EventDispatcher::Dispatch()` calls `EventTargetChainItem::ActivationBehavior()` after the full dispatch cycle. This calls `EventTarget::ActivationBehavior()` on the activation target:\\n- `HTMLInputElement::ActivationBehavior()` (`dom/html/HTMLInputElement.cpp`): Handles checkbox toggling, radio button selection, file picker opening, form submission\\n- `HTMLButtonElement::ActivationBehavior()` (`dom/html/HTMLButtonElement.cpp`): Handles form submission/reset\\n- `HTMLAnchorElement::GetEventTargetParent()` (`dom/html/HTMLAnchorElement.cpp`): Sets up link navigation via `GetEventTargetParentForAnchors()`\\n\\nIf the event's default was prevented (`nsEventStatus_eConsumeNoDefault`), `LegacyCanceledActivationBehavior()` is called instead to undo any pre-activation state changes.\\n\\n### Summary of Key Files\\n\\n| Phase | File | Key Function |\\n|-------|------|--------------|\\n| Entry point | `layout/base/PresShell.cpp` | `PresShell::HandleEvent()` |\\n| Target identification | `layout/base/PresShell.cpp` | `PresShell::GetEventTargetContent()`, `PresShell::EventHandler::DispatchEventToDOM()` |\\n| Pre-dispatch | `dom/events/EventStateManager.cpp` | `EventStateManager::PreHandleEvent()` |\\n| Chain building | `dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp` | `EventDispatcher::Dispatch()` |\\n| Chain traversal | `dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp` | `EventTargetChainItem::HandleEventTargetChain()` |\\n| Target parent resolution | `dom/base/FragmentOrElement.cpp` | `nsIContent::GetEventTargetParent()` |\\n| Listener invocation | `dom/events/EventListenerManager.cpp` | `HandleEventInternal()`, `HandleEventSingleListener()` |\\n| Post-dispatch default | `dom/events/EventStateManager.cpp` | `EventStateManager::PostHandleEvent()` |\\n| Activation behavior | `dom/html/HTMLInputElement.cpp` | `HTMLInputElement::ActivationBehavior()` |\\n| Activation behavior | `dom/html/HTMLButtonElement.cpp` | `HTMLButtonElement::ActivationBehavior()` |\\n| Event creation | `dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp` | `EventDispatcher::CreateEvent()` |\"\n}\n",

Here is the complete flow:\\n\\n### 1. Event Creation\\n\\nA click event originates as a `WidgetMouseEvent` (defined in `widget/MouseEvents.h`). When the widget layer receives a native mouse click, it creates a `WidgetMouseEvent` with message `ePointerClick` (or `eMouseUp` leading to a click). The corresponding DOM-level `MouseEvent` object (in `dom/events/MouseEvent.cpp` / `dom/events/MouseEvent.h`) is created lazily during dispatch via `EventDispatcher::CreateEvent()` in `dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp`.\\n\\n### 2. Event Target Identification\\n\\nThe raw event enters the Gecko event system through `PresShell::HandleEvent()` in `layout/base/PresShell.cpp`. Capture, Target, and Bubble Phase Traversal\\n\\n`EventTargetChainItem::HandleEventTargetChain()` (`dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp`) implements the three-phase traversal:\\n\\n**Capture phase**: Iterates from the end of the chain (outermost) down to just above the target (`firstCanHandleEventTargetIdx`), calling `item.HandleEvent()` with `mInCapturePhase=true`.\\n\\n**Target phase**: Calls `targetItem.HandleEvent()` twice \u2014 once for capture listeners and once for bubble listeners at the target node itself.\\n\\n**Bubble phase**: Iterates from the target upward to the outermost node, calling `item.HandleEvent()` with `mInBubblingPhase=true` (only if the event bubbles).\\n\\nAfter the default event group, the chain is traversed again for the **system event group** (chrome/privileged listeners), with `mInSystemGroup=true`.
